And the reduction of the dislocation is that you place the patient's arm joint on a table and make them extend their arm. The doctor then places their hand or palm over the vicinity of the joint and gently push it back into its proper place.
But moreover, consider whether the palm is already placed on the belly of the hand, then the patient places the back of his hand on a table while extending and reducing; and if dislocation has preceded, place both hands, then the position of the hand of the patient intrinsically on the table, so that the doctor's hand falls over that imminent joint.
And so if it returns quickly, that is good; and otherwise, then strengthen that by applying ointment yielding to the abscess and leave it; and do not repeat this, for if you do, you cannot endure nor perform the reduction of it any longer than a day passes.
But moreover, the joint must be considered according to its tortuosity; and do not note any cause to the patient, but rather that the hand is softened and cannot strengthen any cause; then you know that the nerves are crushed or stretched, and then there is no remedy in it except to apply a cautery near the site and strengthen it with this, giving some relief.
And since the gout has returned, then place it over the ointment which we have recommended, and let it be applied and strengthened for five days; and then dislocate it and leave it, and exercise the hand of the patient.
But if the movement in it has been obstructed and occurs with some gravity, then ease that by applying water compresses and some friction, until it is alleviated.
Chapter XXIX.
On the cure of dislocation of fingers.
In some cases, the fingers are completely dislocated at once.
And when one of the fingers is dislocated at the base of the palm or in the flesh of the finger, then hold the finger and push the dislocation back with your thumbs until it returns to place.
Then hold the tip of the finger, and suspend that part which is dislocated, leaving it for two days.
Then suspend that part and extend it until the finger is properly aligned on that same day.
And when it is night, hold it according to that narration, and do not cease to straighten and exercise it with movement during the day and at night; and do this for several days until it is properly set.
And make it seem as if you are doing so, even if dislocated in the hand, hold that part and do your first operation, until it is healed.
And make it seem as if you are doing so when it is dislocated in other parts.
Capitol.
For the treatment of dislocation of the cervical spine.
When dislocation occurs in any of the vertebrae of the back or the neck, and many vertebrae around that area are displaced, then there is no cure for that part, and death may occur to the patient.
The sign of this is that the patient's excretion is forced out against their will, and they cannot retain it; often, several members of the patient or parts of their legs or arms, or one of those, are softened. Or a vertebra in its place is displaced, as many vertebrae are displaced and many vertebrae are removed to four parts.
Then it is already mended at the rear parts and is named gelbozitation.
May the cure of it be that when you consider whether the gelbozitation arises from purisssia, for in that case there is neither cure nor does one become whole.
May it be that in those arising from coagulation or percussion or similar to those, the Ancients have already spoken of the methods of cure at length, of which the most returns to prophecy; but I will now abbreviate what is necessary from that, for which I have exposed and formed my exposition close to the understanding, with which I have here expanded and clarified it.
And of those, only the one that arises in the two specifically where I advise is cured.
And the patient should be extended on his back close to the wall, and laid out so that he does not touch the feet of others.
And place a straight stick, placed in the ground at the end of the hand near its head, and another stick vertically under his feet at the other end of the stick.
The minister should hold the stick, and it should not be fixed in the ground; another minister should hold the other end according to that form.
And wrap around the head of the patient and tie the lion's hide tightly. Extend the end of the ligament to the stick which should be at the head of the patient, and fasten that in place. And firmly tie the other ligaments under the patient's hips and thighs, extending those to the other stick which should be at the feet of the patient. Adjust all the ligaments and fasten those to the other stick at the feet of the patient.
And the minister should firmly extend the ligament to the part of the stick, and do not loosen the two sticks and the ligaments in which they are placed, but do not fix them as we have said.
And the doctor places his palms on the spine with strength so that it returns, or he places one hand on a table and adjusts his feet on the table as it returns.
And if it does not return in this way, then take a table of which the width or length is about three bracci, and cut into the wall that we said was near the hernia a place at the edge of the table. And place the majority of the table on the spine, and the doctor places his feet on the other edge, and presses well so that the spine is compressed and returns to its place.
And if you wish, turn the part that is twisted with your hand; and when you are on the ground, place the patient's head at the heel of two sticks, the length of which is one braccio, and place his head at the heel of two sticks in the same manner; and make sure the distance between each stick is a palm. Then draw the torn part through the hole in one stick, and secure each stick firmly to the ground so they do not move.
And there should be a round staff on which the cord is wound, and it should be turned in the two grooves of the two staffs.
And at the end of it is a groove in which the staff is wound, the length of which is one palm's breadth where it is wound; and in the other two staffs it is similar to that.
And then strengthen the ligaments you have stretched on the foot in the groove of the staff, and the ligaments you have stretched on the thighs in the cord where you place its ends.
And then place each cord and have a minister hold the cord with his hand, and the doctor tighten the spine as we have said.
And when the spine is returned and the area is tightened, then cover with a paste of honey, and some wool; then place a piece of cloth from a table, whose width be about three fingers or slightly more, and its length enough to cover the part of the spine, and over the portion of the spine.
And then apply the incense which we have mentioned, and use the patient of subtle nourishment under which it is healed.
And if there is any danger at the place at the end of the healing, then ensure that medicines that mollify and soothe are administered through long-term use, which we have recommended; and already a sheet of lead is being administered in that place.
And sometimes dangers occur at the end of the vertebrae of the spine, and are caused by that dislocation; and it is that bone for which you already fear that no suspicion should arise about it with this medicine, as it will greatly harm you.
Chapter XXXI.
On the treatment of dislocated hip.
Know that the hip joint and the joint of the muscle should only be dislocated to such an extent, and not occur in those cases where small movement and depression happen to other joints.
The joint of the ankle is dislocated according to four manners; it can be dislocated inward, outward, forward, or backward.
It is mostly dislocated inward, and little forward or backward.
The sign of dislocation inward is that when you adjust the leg of the healthy side against the affected side, the unhealthy one becomes longer and the heel more prominent than the healthy one. The affected foot cannot bend its toe; this is the place where you should cauterize the apostema, so that the head of the swelling is already reached here.
The sign of the one on which dislocation occurs outward is that the symptoms of it are contrary to this accident.
The sign of dislocation forward is that the leg expands symmetrically, but it cannot bend at all where the pain is in the heel. If forced to move forward, it cannot do so; his urine is retained and swelling occurs, and you should treat him by cauterization on the sole.
And the sign of those to whom dislocation occurs at the back parts is that they do not expand the flank, nor can they bend what is in front so that it bends backwards, and their waist is shorter than the other side, and the flanks are softened, and the apex of the thigh is deviated from that place.
The main reduction of the species of this dislocation is that you consider, at that time, if the dislocation is old and already accustomed, you have almost administered the reduction of it according to its disposition; then there is no need for total treatment in that case; hence, one should not guess at that.
For the one where the dislocation is recent and belongs to one of the four species of dislocation, you should turn the joint and extend it both inward and outward, and manipulate it on the right and left sides, as it will return with force and does not require any other treatment.
Moreover, if it does not return in this manner, you should prepare a strong counterforce and extend the waist on the side that is more injured, or on their hands, or with linseed which is soaked over the flank below the flank; another counterforce should extend the hand from above so that it touches the base of their hands. Then place another person to hold tightly the end of the linseed.
And it is an extension from his arm or from the inner part to the shoulder blade, or from the back to the buttock.
And it is the extension of all these in one go, lifting the patient's limb from his body and letting it dangle.
And this type of extension is common for all four.
And so, if the dislocation returns as we have said, it will be good; otherwise, for each type, what I say about its own treatment is necessary.
In the reduction of its own, when dislocated, and the dislocation is in the inner parts, ensure that the patient's limb is repositioned over his side; then place the bandages around the hip at that location where between the head of the hip bone and where the loin is attached; further extend the bandage from above the shoulder blade to the next part of the scapula.
And further, another minister firmly take hold of the thighs, and compress the thick part of the affected hip, extending it outward by strong extension, so that it returns to its proper place.
And this species is of a milder cure for which that member is reduced compared to other species.
And if it is excused for you and you do not follow the training on this species of cure, then make sure that both feet of the patient are tied together firmly but gently, over both the ankles and both the toes.
And let the length of each be by the quantity of four fingers, and let the patient's leg be extended more than the other by a quantity of two fingers.
And then place the patient's foot on the stake's head, and let it be in the hand; and let the length of the foot from the ground be the quantity of two braces.
And command a strong youth to hold down the thigh, and place the patient's foot on another strong youth, and the other youth holding down the thigh with force, for the joint returns to its place quickly.
And in the reduction itself, when dislocation is at the outer part, make sure that the patient's foot is placed on a pillow according to what we have recommended for having the thigh strong. And strengthen the bandage over the patient's leg and its ankle.
And then two sticks are placed aside, one on the foot and the other on the head; and then sticks adjusted in the middle of the stake fixed under which wet sheets be wrapped, so that the patient is not harmed because the stick is between the thighs of him, for you must allow the extension to the parts left undone.
And then each minister extends to his part, and the doctor with his hand equalizes the reduction according to the art.
And when the dislocation is in the anterior parts, then make sure that the leg is extended slightly, and this is according to this method as narrated for the stake; and the doctor places the palm of his right hand on the affected knee, and then tightens it with the other hand, and by this tightening, he extends the previously bent part to the posterior part.
If the dislocation is at the rear parts, then do not allow the patient to lie on these parts, and elevate them above the ground; it should be laid on a hard surface, just as if the width of him were dislocated to the front parts, according to what we have said about his lying on two widths; and it should be placed with its face and limbs extended, as we have said, not otherwise.
A compression should be applied on the area where the joint is dislocated.
So, when the reduction is completed as it should — and you notice the sign of the reduction, which is that you can extend both limbs of the patient, and when you feel them equal and the limb returns to its normal position; then adjust the thighs and wrap tightly with a bandage so that the width is not altered in any part; and adhere the limb to rest for three or four days.
Then remove the bandage, and compare one limb with the other.
When you see the equal marks in the wound, then know that the dislocation is already healed, and then let the patient go.
And if you see any cause of swelling, then return and apply a poultice to that area, and extend it according to your first structure, and let it remain for three days.
Then loosen that, and allow it to remain in motion over each part for some days, until it is comforted.
Capitol.xxxii.
On the treatment of dislocation of the shoulder.
The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: it can be dislocated to the outer parts, to the inner parts, and to the back parts more than to the front parts; and it is not dislocated to the front parts.
And the sign of shoulder dislocation is that when you command the patient to apply their hand to their hip; then you know that the shoulder is dislocated.
And the restoration of all manners of it is that you make a straight cut in the side, attempt to extend its cavity as much as possible; attach your two fingers to the face of it, and place his foot between your feet; then make sure to adhere the back to your palms, hold those between your thumbs over the back of it with strength, and another minister extend his foot so that the back returns to its place.
And the sign of its submission is that its cavity adheres to the flank easily without effort.
And then apply that and make the cavity adhere to the flank, and place those constantly with a bandage for three or four days, and then remove those.
And do not use the side for ambulation for some days until it is healed and comforted.
But if the reduction of it is excused to you, then administer strong extension to the ligaments of which in the cure of the hip the preceding narrative was told.
Chapter XXXIII.
Of the treatment of dislocation of the ankle.
The ankle is sometimes reduced by slight movement, and sometimes dislocated by force, and the dislocation of the ankle is caused either on the inner side or on the outer side.
And the sign of the ankle dislocation is that you see the ankle swollen from the side where it is dislocated.
More so, the treatment of the reduction of the ankle is by gentle manipulation, and it should be extended with ease and returned to its normal position.
More so, in the treatment of the ankle when dislocated by force, make sure to straighten the limb, and have a strong and brave assistant behind the foot at the midpoint.
And then place your right hand on the upper part of the foot, and with your left hand, hold the lower part of the foot at the location of the heel.
And then pull the foot to your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, and then extend your left hand; and push the foot to the right you straighten the leg.
And do this twice as we have counted.
And then push the foot to the third time towards the leg, and you are at the ankle.
So if it returns in one or two pushes using this method, and if you close the foot properly, that is good; otherwise, then repeat the operation, for it may not return.
But if reducing the foot as we have advised is prohibited to you, then place the leg on a board on the ground, and insert a piece of wood in the ground firmly, so that it fits between the patient's thighs, and you have wrapped a cloth around it to prevent the foot from slipping.
And then the minister should hold their thighs, and another minister extend the foot with their hands or a cloth tied around the leg of the foot; and then each minister extend themselves against the extension of their part, so that the piece of wood remains between the patient's thighs holding it, to prevent the body from being pulled towards the sides as you straighten its extension.
And then the doctor equalizes the dislocation with his hands, while another assistant holds the healthy thigh at the place left vacant, so that the dislocation returns easily.
And then since the dislocation returns and the health of the reduction is declared to you, then apply a strong paste externally there, and bind the foot with lint to the leg.
And beware of the nerves behind the ankle, lest the lint be too strong and severely irritate them.
And leave it there for two or three days; and if the lint is moistened, change it.
And remove it on the third day or fourth, and prohibit the patient from walking for forty days. But if it is necessary for the patient to walk before this time, then there is no guarantee that the dislocation has not become dissolved and corrupted, and that it does not receive healing.
And if an abscess occurs at the wound, then beware that you administer in the treatment of it what we have described in our narrative, in another place for healing and application, until it is fully healed.
Chapter XXXIV.
For the treatment of dislocation of the toes of the feet.
First, ensure that what is dislocated can be reduced with slight extension; and what is not difficult, should be done gently.
But if the dislocation is in some toe joints of the foot, then you should place the patient's foot on a level part of the ground or on a table, and let it be thus as if walking.
Then stand on the patient's foot, and place your own foot over the area near the joints, and press that part with your foot to help it return to its proper position, and observe that it is reduced and does not appear as a prominence in the area.
Then place the patient's foot on a table that can hold the entire foot, which has two supports, and strengthen it with a sturdy structure for three days; then remove it and allow the foot to rest by walking for several days, until it is strengthened and its recovery is assured.
Chapter 35.
Of the species of dislocation that are caused by trauma or fracture or any other means.
When any of these causes occur, and you are involved in the treatment and restoration of it, mistakes can lead to death.
And for this reason, one must not presume in the treatment of it, but rather someone who is skilled in the art, long accustomed to its use, merciful and pious; who waits, not impatient, nor fiery, nor presumptuous; and who uses at the beginning of medicines that cauterize abscesses only, leaving the illness to divine judgment, but to one to whom you hope for salvation from perdition, from the illness alleviation, and in which you appear to have some hope. And then strive to perform the reduction at the beginning of the cause, before it develops into an abscess.
And then, if the limb returns as we want, proceed to administer treatment that cauterizes the abscess and treats the trauma with what is suitable for it from the drying ointments.
And if dislocation or fracture of separated bones occurs, then you must realign their joint, and do so as we have said in the simple ailments that precede these in the places mentioned.
And guard and avoid according to your virtue that of the instrument in the ways of fear according to which my preaching precedes you; for this is better to you from your Creator, and more permanent to your glory, and more greetings to your true essence those in your time. Thus you finish the words of Albucasim perfectly, for which may God be blessed. Amen.
